Main Topics and Facts Presented

  1. Introduction:

    • The article analyzes the 2025 hog market, focusing on price fluctuations and their impact on farmers, the agricultural economy, and consumer livelihoods.
    • It examines current market conditions and forecasts trends for the second half of 2025.

  2. 2025 Hog Price Trends (First Half):

    • Prices showed a downward trend, with the national average pork price dropping 11.4% from 22.81 yuan/kg (Jan 6) to 20.22 yuan/kg (Jun 25).
    • Live hog prices fell 11.8% from the start of the year to 14.61 yuan/kg in June (third week), a 20.8% year-on-year decline.
    • Seasonal factors (e.g., Spring Festival demand) caused brief price spikes, but oversupply led to a prolonged slump.
    • By late June, prices stabilized slightly due to policy interventions (e.g., reduced slaughter weights, discouragement of speculative stocking).

  3. Comparison with 2024:

    • 2024 prices were higher, peaking at 27.77 yuan/kg in May 2024, with an annual average of 16.81 yuan/kg.
    • 2025 prices were lower due to ample supply and weaker seasonal demand.

  4. Supply-Side Factors:

    • Reduced breeding sow inventories: Major farms cut sow stocks by 8â€“10%, which may reduce hog supply by Q2 2026.
    • Decline in speculative stocking ("äºŒè‚²"): Fewer farmers held hogs for future sales, increasing immediate supply and pressuring prices.

  5. Demand-Side Factors:

    • Seasonal consumption boosts: Expected rise in demand from graduation banquets (Julyâ€“August) and holidays (Mid-Autumn, National Day, New Year).
    • Weak overall consumption: Pork demand remained sluggish, with 2025 projected consumption down 2.9% YoY.

  6. Policy Influences:

    • Price stabilization measures: Government pork reserves (e.g., 50,000 tons in May, 30,000 tons in June) aimed to curb excessive price drops.
    • Regulatory controls: Policies restricted large farms from expanding production and encouraged capacity reduction.

Key Data and Statistics

  • Price Changes (2025 H1):

    • Pork: 20.22 yuan/kg (Jun 25) vs. 22.81 yuan/kg (Jan 6) (â€“11.4%).
    • Live hogs: 14.61 yuan/kg (Jun, Week 3) vs. 16.55 yuan/kg (start of year) (â€“11.8%).

Primary Conclusions (Second-Half 2025 Forecast)

  1. Potential Price Increases:

    • Reduced supply: Breeding cuts may tighten supply by Q4 2025.
    • Seasonal demand: Holidays and year-end cured meat demand could boost prices.
    • Policy support: Government interventions (reserves, subsidies) may stabilize prices.

  2. Downside Risks:

    • Persistent oversupply: High slaughter volumes may continue pressuring prices.
    • Weak consumption: Economic factors could limit demand recovery.

  3. Overall Outlook:

    • Prices may stabilize or rise moderately in late 2025, but significant rebounds depend on supply adjustments and demand recovery.
